=500  \\$avery rare dutch songbook. For the music to his poems Starter made use of old english tunes.
=500  \\$aStarter (Jan Jansz.), a poet from Friesland who flourished in the first half of the seventeenth century, published several works of poetry, but mostly of frolicsome and lascivious content; some stage work by him is also available. He died young in battle. As he had to deal with ecclesiastical opposition, his plays were banned. Also his publishing company went down. In 1625 he became the historian of Count Ernst van Mansfelt. He also took on the task of 'courantier', which meant collecting war news and passing it on. It is in this war, the Thirty Years' War, that he dies while marching in Mansfelt's campaign in Hungary.
Many of his poems became the subject of other artworks such as plays or paintings. He is best known for his poem about the "Mennonite Sister".
=500  \\$aContains 10 charming & beautiful engravings by Jan van de Velde II (ca. 1593-1641), interesting both for the costumes and manners of the period: Frontispiece is depicting the city of Leeuwarden as a joyful pleasure garden (Fountain with Frisian virgin: a fountain in the middle of a square that represents the Frisian virgin. She holds the weapon of Friesland in her hand. Amor is on her lap, his arm around her neck. Around the fountain elegant couples that dance, hiking, ministo, making music, etc. On a Banderolder ceased by Putti is listed the title of the book), and introduction is illustrated with engraving  portraying Starter as poet of the lyric of love: The swans symbolize himself and pull Cupido away from 'The Isle of Dogs' (England).
=534  \\$cAmsterdam, Dirc Voscuyl,1621
=561  \\$aEx Libris Christian Ernst Graf zu Stolberg (Illustrated armorial bookplate)
Christian Ernst Graf zu Stolberg (1691-1771).The golden age of the Stolberg library was during the reign of Christian Ernst (1710-1771). He not only greatly increased its holdings and opened it to the public, but was also its librarian, commissioning the distinctive Stolberg bookplate and personally inscribing the publication date on the spine of each volume bound in white vellum. In 1746 Christian Ernst issued an edict making the collection—by then about 10,000 volumes—a public library.
=590  \\$aDen tweeden druck op nieuws vermeerdert ende verbetert, met verscheyden dichten ende liedekens, soo geestige als boertige, door Ian Iansz. Starter. SS. LL. ST. Mitsgaders oock noch vermeert ende verçierd met schoone kopere figuren ende by alle onbekende wysen de noten, ofte musycke gevoeght.

=100  \\$aRinck, Christian Heinrich$d1770-1846$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q559451$96535
=245  \\$aNeues Choralbuch für das Großherzogthum Hessen
=260  \\$aOffenbach am Main$bAndré$c1814
=300  \\$axviii-100-xx pages$b16x23 cm, oblong
=336  \\$anotated music
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aorgan accompaniment for a collection of 138 chorales
=500  \\$aRinck comes from a family of teachers. From 1786, he received organ and composition lessons from a pupil of Johann Sebastian Bach, by Johann Christian Kittel (1732-1809) in Erfurt. In 1805 he moved to Darmstadt and become cantor and organist at the city church. Later he was employed as court organist and chamber musician of Grand Duke Louis I of Hesse-Darmstadt. 
Rinck was known early on as an excellent organist and was much in demand as an expert.His organ compositions were highly appreciated and his "Praktische Orgelschule", op. 55 was a leading method in Germany until the 20th century. Rinck made an important contribution to the renewal and improvement of Protestant organ music at the beginning of the 19th century.

=500  \\$aGuitar tablature with dance music. As Nigel North informed us, the first twenty and last nineteen pages of music are conceived for a five-course guitar. Twenty-six intermediary pages are dedicated to an 11-course lute
=500  \\$aMss contains 47 solos for five-course guitar tuned a d b e' and 28 solos for eleven-course lute in D-minor tuning.
=500  \\$aThe family of Sinzendorf (also: Sinzendorff) was a Bavarian-Austrian noble family
=500  \\$aThis is one of the music manuscripts from the family library of count Leopold Goëss. Most of them were kept at the family home in Ebenthal Castle in Carinthia (Austria), this manuscript belonged at least until 1997 to the library of the Landesmuseum Klagenfurt.

=590  \\$aOder gantz natürliche Abbildung solcher Gelehrten, die da vermeynen alle Gelehrsamkeit und Wissenschafften verschlucket zu haben, auch in dem Wahn stehen, daß ihres gleichen nicht auf Erden zu finden, wannenhero sie alle andere Menschen gegen sich verachten, einen unerträglichen Stoltz und Hochmuth von sich spüren lassen; in der That aber doch selber so, wie sie in ihrer Haut stecken, Ignoranten, Pedanten, ja Ertz-Fantasten und tumme Sympel sind, die von der wahren Gelehrsamkeit, womit die Weisheit verknüpffet seyn muß, weit entfernet. Nebst einer lustigen Dedication und sonderbaren Vorrede. =041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aHuygens, Constantijn$d1596-1687$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q560746$95174
=245  \\$aBatava Tempe:$b't Voor-hout van 's Graven-Hage
=260  \\$aMiddelburg$bVan der Hellen$bVan de Venne$c1622
=300  \\$a31pages$billustrations
=500  \\$aOne of the two collections with which Constantijn Huygens (1596-1687) broke through as a poet
=500  \\$a2 remarkable engravings included: title page (elaborate printers-logo) and first page (town-view of the Voorhout square in The Hague).
=501  \\$aBound in with 'Kerkuraia mastix' and 'Groete aen de ioffrouwen'
=520  \\$aThe title of this great work of poetry, 'Batava Tempe', an ode to a beautiful and famous street in the old city centre of The Hague, the Lange Voorhout, accurately conveys the content. The word Tempe is derived from a beautiful valley in northern Greece, Thessaly to be precise, which was so called in antiquity. Apparently Huygens relates this beautiful valley to the Voorhout in The Hague. So the poem is about the Voorhout, which is also called Batave Tempe and is located in The Hague. Constantijn Huygens could also have chosen another place to write a great poem about, but apparently the Voorhout surpassed all other places and played the most important role for him in his life.

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aHuygens, Constantijn$d1596-1687$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q560746$95174
=245  \\$aKerkuraia mastix,$bsatyra, dat is, 't Costelick mal
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aMiddelburg$bvan der Hellen$bvan de Venne$c1622
=300  \\$a[viii]-19 pages$billustrations
=500  \\$aDedicated "Aen de Heere Iacob Cats, Raedt ende Pensionaris der Stadt Middelburgh"
=500  \\$aOne of the two collections with which Huygens broke through as a poet
=500  \\$aApart from J. De Brune, (the elder), 3 more threshold poems by F.C. [= Jacob Cats], I. Luyt and I. A. F. are included.
=500  \\$a2 remarkable engravings included: title page (elaborate printers-logo) and first page (poor family scene).
=501  \\$aBound in with 'Batava Tempe' and 'Groete aen de ioffrouwen'
=520  \\$aIn 1621-1622 Huygens wrote the poem "Κερκυραία μάστιξ, Satyra,'t Costelijk mal" ('Costly folly'), a satire on the aping of foreign fashions by the young people of The Hague.  The two words in Greek translate literally as 'Corcyraean scourge'. This was an extremely elaborate scourge described in detail by the Greek geographer & philosopher Strabo (Geography, VII, Fragments, 4). Strabo concludes his discussion of the phrase by stating that it was a proverbial term. Huygens uses it to refer to the overly elaborate or superfluous ornament and clothing worn by the young people of The Hague.

=100  \\$aLustig, Jacob Wilhelm$d1706-1796$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1677671$95820
=245  \\$aSamenspraaken over muzikaale beginselen
=246  \1$aTwaalf redeneeringen over nuttige muzikaale onderwerpen
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bOlofsen$c1756
=300  \\$a12 vols. in 1 (699-[31] pages)$b20 inserted folded pages plates with musical examples and illustrations
=500  \\$aCited in Koopman 1985, p. 16 and Koopman 2016, 675 (Jacob Wilhelm Lustig [1706-1796] being one of his favorite authors: "he wrote in Dutch beautifully"). 
‘Ton Koopman on bookcollecting’ In: Notes, Quarterly Journal of the Music Library Association Vol.72 No.4 ed. D. Campana (2016).
'Barokmuziek: Theorie en praktijk', Utrecht/Antwerpen, 1985.

=504  \\$aIncludes an index
=590  \\$averhandelende: 1) Algemeene beginselen; 2) Het waare oogmerk van 't ut, re, mi enz.; 3-4) De grondtoonen der kerkpsalmen; 5) Het regte gebruik van zangmuziek; 6) Den oorsprong der zangkonst; 7) Het wezen der muziek; 8) Den muzikaalen smaak; 9) De muzikaale dichtkunde; 10) Een nieuw intervallen systeem; 11) De muzikaale harmony, en 12) De volmaakte behandeling der kerkzangen. ... Ten onderzoek van kenners, ter verlustiging van geoefende en ter onderrigting van onkundige weetgierige muziek-liefhebbers, meerder klaar- en bevalligheids-halve in de form van maandelyksche samenspraaken opgesteld

=100  \\$aZehentner, Paul$d1589-1648$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q55874362$97979
=245  \\$aPromontorium malæ spei: impiis periculose navigantibus propositum
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aHaupt; Widmanstadt$bGraz$c1643
=300  \\$a[xxxviii]-752-[10] pages$bgilt edges, 2 engravings
=336  \\$abook
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aJesuit warning of the consequences of licentiousness ("Promontory, thoughts of hope for the wicked goal that sailed dangerously. Whether it is a sign of rejection and note: procrastination of repentance written precautionary men's amendment is reluctance, sometimes hope to repent.")
=500  \\$aFirst and only edition of a Latin edifying text on moral and religious issues by the Jesuit Paul Zehentner (1589-1648), preacher at the Graz court of the widow of the Holy Roman Emperor Ferdinand II and teacher of grammar, the humanities and the Holy Scripture at Millestadt in Austria. A moral-theological treatment of state theory, astrology and magic, intended to highlight the dangers of licentious behaviour. 
=500  \\$aIt provides our first known reference to the tragedy of Leontius, a play Zehentner saw at the Jesuit University in Ingolstadt in 1615, and which was to serve as a prototype for the Don Juan legend (Keefe, Mozart studies, p. 140). 
=500  \\$aZehentner dedicated the book to Leonardus Helfridus, Count at Maggau, 26 October 1643, and received a privilege from the Holy Roman Emperor Ferdinand III.
=500  \\$aEngraved allegorical frontispiece and a richly designed armorial and emblematic dedication plate, both by David Tscherning.

=590  \\$aSive, signum & nota reprobationis: procrastinatio poenitentiae, scripta cautelae hominum, emendatione[m] vita[e] cunctantium, spe aliquando resipiscendi.

=500  \\$aIn 1822 Logier was called to Berlin to help found a music academy, and subsequently trained elementary teachers on behalf of the king until 1826. In addition, the publishing house of his brother Wilhelm published his textbooks in German.  In this method, several pupils are taught at a time, with technical instruction done together with instruction in principles of harmony. This lay the basis of group teaching in music.

=100  \\$aRoyer, Pancrace$d1705-1755$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1682344$97027
=245  \\$aZaide, Reine de Grenade. Ballet héroïque
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bs.n.$c1739
=300  \\$a[iv]-114-[2] pages$bleather bound, embossed gilded spine, marbled endpapers
=500  \\$aZaïde was first performed, under the direction of the composer, on 3 September 1739 for the wedding of King Louis XV's daughter, when it ran for 44 performances, and was revived for the wedding of the Dauphin in 1745, and again for the wedding of Marie Antoinette in 1770.

=041  \\$afre$hita
=059  \\$av 2ob 2hrn 2vn vla bc
=100  \\$aDuni, Egidio$d1708-1775$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q953519$95418
=245  \\$aLe Peintre amoureux de son modéle.$bOpéra-comique en 2 actes mêlé d'ariettes
=260  \\$aParis$bDuni$c1758
=300  \\$a[ii]-97-[1]-4-17 pages
=500  \\$aUnder Goldoni's influence, Duni made contact with the director of the Opéra-comique in Paris, Jean Monnet. At first, Monnet was not very enthusiastic about the idea of entrusting the composition of a French opera to an Italian composer, but then he agreed and suggested a text by Louis Anseaume: Le Peintre amoureux de son modèle. The resulting opéra comique by Duni was premiered in July 1757 with brilliant success. The composer then moved permanently to Paris, where he remained until his death.
=500  \\$asee 15B10 for arias from this opera

The price is nevertheless even lower than that of the poorest and least careful of the former editions. The Editor ventures to issue them at this price, solely in the hope of thereby rendering these glorious masterpieces accessible to all, as a welcome companion in the concert-room, and a treasure and ornament for the home."

=245  \\$aA. S. J. Dekker, kerkorgelbouwers Goes
=260  \\$aGoes$bDekker$c19xx
=300  \\$a[16 pages]$bbound in light cardboard, tight together with a ribon, inserted leaflet, silver embossed and engraved frontcover
=500  \\$aAnton Samuel Jan Dekker (1869-1918) opened a small repair shop in Goes in 1892; he also did trade in organs. From 1906, Dekker made his own organs. After 1918, the business was continued by his sons Jacobus Cornelis (1900-1969) and Jan Adriaan (1902-1991). The organ department, which had initially flourished in the pre-war years, gradually became secondary and died a quiet death after the Second World War.

=245  \\$aPrincipes de musique.$bDivisez en quattre parties
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aParis$bMontéclair$c1736

=500  \\$aCited in Koopman, Barokmuziek: Theorie en praktijk (Utrecht/Antwerpen, 1985), p.15
=590  \\$aLa Premiere Partie Contient tout ce qui appartient à l'Intonation. La II.me Partie Tout ce qui regarde la Mesure et le Mouvement. La III.e Partie La Maniere de joindre les paroles aux nottes et de bien former les agréments du chant. La IV.e Partie Est l'Abregé d'un nouveau systême de Musique, par lequel l'Auteur fait voir qu'en changeant peu de choses dans la maniere de notter la Musique, on en rendoit l'Etude et la pratique plus aisées. Composez et dediez a S.A.S. Monseigneur le Prince de Carignan

=500  \\$aFerdinand was the son of Guillaume Staes, organist at the Brussels royal chapel. From 1758, Ferdinand Staes had lessons from his father and later from Ignaz Vitzthumb. He worked as harpsichordist at the Théâtre de la Monnaie in Brussels. In 1767, he was appointed assistant to his father (second organist at the royal chapel). In 1772, Ferdinand Staes became organist at the Madeleine church in Brussels.

=500  \\$aIn 1775 Swinburne toured Spain with fellow Catholic Sir Thomas Gascoigne, an account was published in 1779, then, reunited with his family, "sailed to Naples and from 1777 until early 1779 toured the Kingdom of the Two Sicilies. =520  \\$a"Reicha was appointed professor of counterpoint and fugue at the Conservatoire in 1818. His Cours de composition musicale, ou Traité … d’harmonie pratique, published about 1816-18, replaced Catel’s treatise [Traité d'harmonie, 1802; see 07E73], which had been the official one since 1802. One of the first modern classroom harmony textbooks using examples written expressly for the text, the Cours de composition deals with harmony (tempering the proscription against 5ths and octaves), strict and free music, imitation and orchestration. It stresses the point that theory must be justified by practice and that the pupil must learn about contemporary usage, not solely about ancient principles that diametrically opposed what he heard outside the classroom; these ‘ancient principles’ caused many students to believe wrongly that serious study of composition was useless because free music permitted anything." (Peter Eliot Stone in the New Grove Dictionary of Music & Musicians)

=245  \\$aUmständliche Geschichte der Kaiserl. und des Heil. Römischen Reichs freyen Stadt Lübeck$nvol. 1

=500  \\$aJohann Rudolph Becker (1736-1815) was an administrative lawyer in the service of the city of Lübeck, who achieved fame as a writer and historian.
=500  \\$aHis main work is a comprehensive chronicle of the city of Lübeck, which, due to its political importance and the large number of historians who had been active before him since the time of its foundation, had a good source of information. The 'Umständliche Geschichte der Kaiserl. und des Heil. Römischen Reichs freyen Stadt Lübeck' was printed at his own expense. The first two volumes were published in 1782 and 1784, covering the period from the beginnings to the Peace of Westphalia.

=041  \\$adut
=100  \\$aWilp, Sara Maria van der$d1716-1803$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q19802259$4aut$98041
=245  \\$aGedichten
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aAmsterdam$bMeijer$c1772
=300  \\$a[10]-296-[4] pages$bbound in marbled cardboard, linen spine, engraved frontispiece and title page, untrimmed edges
=500  \\$aThe book contains a variety of poems, including love poems, religious poems and poems about nature. The poems reflect the style and language of the end of the 18th century. Van Der Wilp is considered one of the most important female poets in Dutch literary history. Her work has been praised as much for its poetic qualities as for its feminism, as she was one of the few female writers of her time to openly express her views on women's rights. This book is therefore not only a collection of beautiful poems, but also an important historical document that gives us insight into the literary and social context of the 18th century.
=500  \\$aIn Dutch art history Van Der Wilp became known because of a portrait that Marinkelle had made of her in 1771 and which she replaced with an image more appropriate to her age, plated after Bruyninx by Vinkeles, as the first was engraved by J. Houbraken, while both at the time experienced a rather ambiguous interest.

=500  \\$aA blind 18th century musician based in London, Starling Goodwin wrote music both for church use and public concerts. Surviving examples of his work include voluntaries for organ or harpsichord and a number of popular light entertainment songs. One of the greatest pluralists of his profession, he was organist at four London churches simultaneously at the time of his death. He was also a witty and amusing socialiser and an accomplished violinist.

=245  \\$aMissen en gezangen
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aUtrecht$bWeyde, van der$c1745
=300  \\$a[i]-48-[2] pages
=336  \\$anotated music
=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aThe so-called 'Stukjesboek', which formed the basis of the old Catholic church song in the Netherlands: 98 songs in Latin and Dutch, plus three ordinaria in Latin. Strong Jansenist influence.
=500  \\$aMissen en Gezangen is not the only para-liturgical hymnbook that the Utrecht Church had after the schism of 1723.
Some of the material it contains had already been published in Het Paradijs, which appeared in eight editions between 1621 and 1679 in Antwerp, or in Het Prieel, Brugues 1609/l0. Also the collection of Gulielmus de Swaen, parish priest in Gouda, to which he gave the name Den Singende Swaen'[, -an allusion to his own name, which means 'swan', - contains pieces that can be found in Missen en Gezangen. Of a substantial part, however, the origin remains obscure. No doubt a large repertoire of Latin and Dutch hymns was known from the rather isolated milieu of the Utrecht church. It is even possible that the type of hymns found in Missen en Gezangen and the other collections mentioned, were cherished by the secular clergy and that their use was discouraged, more or less, by the regulars. It is at least curious that in the Old Catholic Church an abundance of hymns have survived, while they are relatively rare in the Roman Catholic Church parishes in Friesland and northern Holland.
=500  \\$aIn Missen en Gezangen we find texts by Andreas van der Schuur and Jean Baptiste Stalpaert van der Wielen , but most of the texts are from the Counter-Reformation period and are anonymous.
=500  \\$aAndreas van der Schuur (also Van der Schuer) (1656- 1719) was ordained a priest in 1680 and became parish priest in Vianen in 1692. Archbishop Van Neercassel entrusted him with the translation of the Bible  in 1732, completed by H. van Rhijn. He was the composer of several religious poems, both Latin and Dutch.


=500  \\$aJean Baptiste Stalpa(e)rt van der Wiele(n) (1579 - 1630), a lawyer in The Hague in 1598,  became a priest in 1606. In 1613 he was appointed parish priest in Delft, where he remained until his death. In 1621 he published "Hemelrijk", in 1622 "Het vrouwelick cieraed van St Agnes", religious poetry. In prose he published "Roomsche Reys" in 1624, and in 1628 a collection of hymns "'t
Gulden Jaer ons'Heeren Jesu Christi". As a posthumous work he published "Extractum Catholicum" and "Guide Jaers Feestdaghen of de Schat der gheestelijekeLofsanghen", in 1631 and 1634. He was the composer of about 2000 hymns.

=100  \\$aBach, Johann Christian$d1735-1782$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q106641$914631
=240  \\$aOp. 1
=245  \\$aSix Concertos Pour le Clavecin ou Harpe, deux violons, et un violoncelle$bOeuvre 1
=260  \\$aParis$bLe Duc
=300  \\$a33 pages
=500  \\$aKeyboard part only.
=500  \\$aJ C Bach’s set of six harpsichord concertos, Opus 1, was published in March 1763 and dedicated to the eighteen-year-old Queen Charlotte, to whom Bach had recently started giving singing lessons. Princess Charlotte Sophie of Mecklenburg-Strelitz had married King George III on 8 September 1761. She was a passionate music lover, and must have valued the opportunity to have lessons in her own language with a musician of Bach’s calibre. Several of her children were also to receive tuition from Bach, including the future kings George IV and William IV, and Queen Charlotte remained a life-long supporter, even arranging for the return journey of Bach’s wife to her native Italy after his death in 1782.
=500  \\$asignature of Le Duc on title-page

=504  \\$acontains a publishers catalogue by Le Duc (two pages)
=563  \\$aEdges of all pages have been restored. New binding in 18th c. style.

=100  \\$aHandel, George Frideric$d1685-1759$4cmp$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q7302$94765
=245  \\$aThe Music in the Alchymist [HWV 43]
=260  \\$aLondon$bArnold$c1787-97
=300  \\$a8 pages
=490  \\$aThe Works of G. F. Händel, Ed. in Score$vplate no. 64
=500  \\$aThe Alchemist, HWV 43, is incidental music used for the revival of Ben Jonson's play The Alchemist at the Queen's Theatre, London on 14 January 1710. The work is an arrangement, by an anonymous composer, of music written by George Frideric Handel.
All but one of the movements were taken from the extended overture to Handel's first Italian opera Rodrigo. The overture introduced the play and the other movements were used to fill the gaps between acts.
The incidental music was published in full a few months after the first performance; however, it is unlikely that Handel received any payment for either the performance or publication of the music. It is likely that the work was the first of Handel's music to be performed in England. 
=501  \\$aBound in with 'Lessons for the Harpsichord First Published in the Year 1720', 'A Second Set of Lessons for the Harpsichord, ‘ A Third Set of Lessons for the Harpsichord’ and ‘Six Fugues or Voluntarys for the Organ or Harpsichord’

=500  \\$aDiffers from the the original to a considerable extent, both removing and adding material. In fact there is probably less material by Geminiani here than by the anonymous editor. Most noticeable are the 24 'Gammes' (scales) for 2 violins (in a similar manner to Baillot's Methode) and the 12 duos; however some of Geminiani's 'Compositions' for violin & continuo, and a few of the 'Essempii/Exemples' are retained. =110  \\$4edt$aAllgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (Switzerland)$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q2648827$921129
=245  \\$aMusicalische Neu-Jahrs-Gedichte von der Music-Gesellschaft auf der Teutschen Schul in Zürich
=260  \\$aZürich$bDeutsche Schule$c1714-40
=300  \\$a224 pages$bmusic, illustrations
=500  \\$aIn the 17th century music in Zürich was dominated by three collegia musica: the first was ‘zum Chorherrensaal’, followed by the ‘ab dem Musiksaal’ (from 1613) and ‘zur deutschen Schule’ (from 1679). Initially they were concerned only with sacred music, but later also performed contemporary German and Italian secular music. The three societies merged in 1812 to form the Allgemeine Musikgesellschaft Zürich (AMGZ), which since 1813 has produced books on musical subjects in a series of ‘Neujahrsblättern’, the successors to a series of New Year collections of polyphonic pieces published by two of the collegia musica from 1685 and 1713 respectively.
=500  \\$aSee 04J20, 04J21, 10B20, 11H13, G1-027 and G1-028 for similar collections
=500  \\$aEach year between 1713 and 1740 has a New Year's poem and a song with an engraved frontispiece (‘Kupfer-Blatt') bound in, numbered I-XXVIII, but paginated continuously
=500  \\$aThe poems and plates deal predominantly with music, e.g. Jubal's invention of music
=500  \\$aMost songs have Cantus I and Bassus on left page, Cantus II and Altus on right page, but some are for two sopranos only, whose parts face each other; still others have a basso continuo (bassus generalis) part for 'organum'

=500  \\$aeach year has an emblematic plate (some depicting musical elements, such as tempi, dynamics  and mythical musicians, others showing sights from Zürich, and yet others featuring musical iconography), followed by a poem, a strophic song and sometimes psalms and/or quotes from the Bible or from writings by Seneca, Breitinger, Saavedra, Augustine, Kircher, Ovid

M. Hudrich Zwinglein, gebührtig in dem Wilden Hause bey St. Johann im Togganburg: henach getreueifrigen Antistitem der lieben Kirchen Zürich, und hochverdienten Hrn. Reformatorem, zur seligen Glaubens-Verbesserung den 1. Tag Jenner im 1519. Jahr Christi glücklich wieder eingeführet, und nun den 1. Tag Jenner des 1719. Jahrs Christi bey einer Kunst- und Tugendliebenden Jugend loblicher Statt Zürich erneueret ware: als dero ein würdiges Lobopfer in den Mund legen wöllen eine ehren-Gesellschaft auf dem neuerbauten Music-Saal"

=041  \\$adut
=245  \\$aCatalogus van eenige raare, door veel moeyten by een gezogte schoone boeken en manuscripten nevens verscheyde fraaye rariteiten van den alomvermaarden en hoog-geleerden Heer Professor Petrus Burmannus
=260  \\$as.l.$bs.n.$c1709
=300  \\$a23 pages
=500  \\$aSatirical catalog of an imaginary library, referring to Burman's affair (Burman was accused of having fathered an illegitimate child), publications of which are included in this binding
=500  \\$aThe Utrecht professor Pieter Burman is portrayed as a frantic hunter of the female gender. The occasion was the lawsuit filed by Dina van Woudenberg against Burman, which had thrown Utrecht into turmoil in 1709. Dina "an inferior female person" had accused Petrus Burmannus, professor of classical languages and history, of deflowering her at the fair in the year 1708. This was a staged attempt by Burman's enemies to discredit him. This history had set many pens in motion. A veritable pamphlet battle ignited. Burman's fondness for the stage in Utrecht had earned him the hatred of a number of orthodox Voetians. He was criticised for the text editions of classical writers, such as Petronius and Terentius, which he provided with philological commentary. The scrapey passages of these texts, explored by him to the bone, were blamed on his horny interests. However, his opponents did not succeed in overthrowing the moral deceiver Burman through their pamphlets. In 1715 when he succeeded Perizonius in Leiden, the pamphlet battle, which had already begun in 1706, came to an end. 
=501  \\$aBound in with 'Proces geventileert voor den Ed: Hove van Utrecht tusschen Dina van Spangen, Wed: van Jan van Woudenberg, als moeder en mombersse over hare onmondige dochter Da van Woudenberg, Imp.ten in cas van defloratie C. Den Heere ende Mr. Petrus Burmannus, Professor in de Academie alhier Ged:', 'Proces geventileert voor den Ed: Gerechte van Utrecht Tusschen Den Heere ende Mr. Petrus Burmannus, Professor in de Academie alhier in cas van Injurien contra den heer Daniel Voet, medicinae Doctor’ and ‘De gewaande weuwenaar, met het bedroge kermis-kind’
=590  \\$aZullende op den 28 van Wynmaant deze jaars by Executie verkocht worden. Gedrukt voor de Koopers.

=100  \\$aSeelen, Johann Heinrich von$d1688-1762$4aut$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q1694556$98132
=245  \\$aIubilæum Lubecense
=260  \\$aLübeck$bSchmid$c1740
=300  \\$a[viii]-64 pages$bTitle page in red and black ink
=500  \\$aVon Seelen was extremely productive as a writer. A list of his writings lists 419 printed works dealing with theological and orientalist as well as pedagogical, local historical, biographical, numismatic and even alchemical topics. As an educator, he reformed the teaching system at the Katharineum Gymnasium zu Lübeck and brought the school to a new level of prestige. He was the first to describe the history of the school. He kept out of the theological disputes of his time. Together with Samuel Gerhard von Melle and Heinrich Scharbau, he published a scientific journal Bibliotheca Lubecensis, which appeared in twelve volumes from 1725-1732, and was also involved in its successor, Nova Bibliotheca Lubecensis (eight volumes 1753-1757). 
=500  \\$aPart 3 contains the lyrics to the music which was played at the jubilant orations held in St. Catherina's Auditorium on september 1st 1740, in grateful remembrance of the 600 year old town of lubeck

=501  \\$aBound in with ‘Q. F. F. Q. S. historia media Lubecensis ab anno MCLXXXII ad annum MCXXVII’, ‘Q. F. F. S. historia media Lubecensis recentior ab anno MCCCXXVII ad annum MCCC’, ‘Q. F. F. Q. S. historia Lubecensis recentior ab anno MCCC ad annum MCCCC’, ‘De origine, incrementis et laudibus Lubecæ elegia’, ‘De Friderici Daniæ et Norvagiæ Principis hereditarii Serenis et Rel. usta et Legitima postulatione in adiutorum episcopatus Lubecensis’ and ‘Notitia maiorum, plurimas Lubecensium, aliorumque clarorum virorum, de ecclesia, republica et literis egregie meritorum vitas’

=245  \\$aCorrespondance (concernant la livraison de vin)
=260  \\$aPérigueux; Couze; Bordeaux; Bergerac$c1795-1829
=300  \\$a75 pages
=500  \\$aCorrespondence addressed to Schröder and Schylen, traders in the Chatrons in Bordeaux (and some others),  dated between the year Germinal 3 (march 1795) and 1829. 53 letters signed for the most part by Desmartis and Choiet, traders in Bergerac (2 from Courtois in Perigueux and 1 from Dumare in Couze) The Correspondence concerns the delivery of wine. 51 postmarks from Bergerac and 2 from Perigueux. (info Antiquarian)
=500  \\$aThe Bergerac & Périgord (Courtois & Couze) were wine-growing regions, a subregion of South West France,  which corresponds roughly to the current  Dordogne Department. Bordeaux, hub of the famed wine-growing region, is a port city on the Garonne River in southwestern France.

=100  \\$aHumphries, John S.$dc. 1707-1733$4cmp$98160
=245  \\$aXII Sonatas for Two Violins with a Through Bass for the Harpsichord op.1
=250  \\$a1st ed.
=260  \\$aLondon$bWalsh$c1728
=300  \\$a20-15-15 pages
=500  \\$aAssessed negatively by John Hawkins in his 'History of the Science and Practice of Music' (1776), vol. 5, p. 366: "in the year 1728 he published by subscription twelve Sonatas for two violins and a bass, of a very original cast, in respect that they are in a style somewhat above that of the common popular airs and country-dance tunes, the delight of the vulgar, and greatly beneath what might be expected from the studies of a person at all acquainted with the graces and elegancies of the Italians in their compositions for instruments. To this it must be attributed that the sonatas of Humphries were the common practice of such small proficients in harmony, as in his time were used to recreate themselves with music at alehouse clubs and places of vulgar resort in the village adjacent to London: Of these there were formerly many, in which six-pence at most was the price of admission."

=590  \\$aN.B. These Sonatas are proper to be play'd with two German Flutes &c.

=500  \\$aBeautiful title-page with lithograph depicting a parade, church interiors and the exterior of St Paul's cathedral: pages 2-3 have it that "This solemn and pathetic composition was written for the Oratorio of Saul in 1738. It was performed at the interment of George the Second, which first originated the custom of making it part of the burial ceremony."'

=245  \\$aSonates pour le violoncelle
=260  \\$as.l.$c18xx
=300  \\$a26 pages
=500  \\$aA mid 18th- or early-19th-century manuscript containing six six sonatas for two violoncellos, with upper staff notated in alto clef. According to Elinor Frey, who inspected the manuscript in Autumn 2023, it is "not immediately appealing music, perhaps [by] an amateur. ... It’s pretty rare to have two-movement sonatas, they all end with the Rondeau (I would place it as German or French sort of "easy" sonata genre, Abel has some of these).

=100  \\$aMengozzi, Bernardo$d1758-1800$4edt$1http://www.wikidata.org/entity/Q19998065$98165
=245  \\$aMéthode de chant du Conservatoire de Musique
=260  \\$aParis$bConservatoire de musique$c1803-4
=300  \\$a[vii]-290-[2] pages
=500  \\$aLargely the work of Bernardo Mengozzi, a member of the commission for preparing the Méthod de chant (cf. Avertissement)
=500  \\$aContains many musical examples by various composers, ranging in length from a few measures of recitative to complete solfèges and arias in vocal score.
The recitatives are by Sacchini (p. 68), Glu[c]k (p. 68-69), and Piccinni (p. 69-70).
The solfèges are by P.P. Colonna (p. 86-87), Bononcini (p. 88-89), Benedetto Marcello (p. 90-91), Hasse (p. 92-94), Galuppi (p. 95-97), Porpora (p. 98-99), A. Scarlatti (p. 100-01), Caffaro [i.e. Cafaro] (p. 102-105), L. Vinci (p. 106-107), L. Leo (p. 108-109), Traetta (p. 110-113), N. Conforto (p. 114-115), D. Alberti (p. 116-117), Jom[m]elli (p. 118-123), Gasparini (p. 124-125), G. Latilla (p. 126-128), Piccinni (p. 129-132), Pergolese (p. 132-133), Manna (p. 134-135), N. Sala (p. 136-138), F. Maio [i.e. Gian Francesco Majo?] (p. 138-143), Costanzi (p. 144-145), Terradellas (p. 146-148), Perez (p. 148-50), M. Vento (p. 150-153), Cimarosa (p. 154-159), G.C. [i.e. Johann Christian] Bach (p. 159-162; this is "Chiari fonti" from the Bach/Guglielmi arrangement of Gluck's Orfeo, without its orchestral introduction and coda; Terry p. 234, no. 2), Sacchini (p. 162-165), Anfossi (p. 165-168), and Sarti (p. 168-172).
The "Choix d'airs de différens caractères" are by Hasse (p. 174-178), L. Leo (p. 178-179 and 188-191), A. Hasse (p. 180-182), Jom[m]elli (p. 182-187, 220-227, 228-232, 236-241, and 254-257), P. Caffaro [i.e. Cafaro] (p. 192-195), N. Piccinni (p. 195-199 and 208-212), A. Sacchini (p. 200-203, 213-219, 232-235, and 268-273), G. [i.e. Johann Christian] Bach (p. 204-207; "La sorte mia spietata," Terry, p. 251, no. 4 (mistranscribed)), S. Sarti (p. 242-247), D. Cimarosa (p. 248-253 and 286-290), J. Maio [i.e. Gian Fancesco Majo or Giuseppe de Majo] (p. 258-263 and 280-285), B. Galuppi (p. 264-267), and T. Traetta (p. 274-279).

=336  \\$aprinted
=500  \\$aYearbook of the Katharineum in Lübeck, a gymnasium famous for its curriculum of the trivium (grammar, rhetoric and logic), the quadrivium (arithmetic, geometry, music, and astronomy), as well as the study of literature, poetry, drama, philosophy, history, art, and languages.


=500  \\$aJohannes Julius Schubring was a German classical scholar and director of the Katharineum in Lübeck 1880-1903.
